<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2350" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg/220px-Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg/330px-Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg/440px-Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Luftbild_Rathaus_Landtag_Marktkirche_Wilhelmstra%C3%9Fe_Kurhaus_Neroberg_Opelbad_Griechische_Kapelle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of Wiesbaden</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Wiesbaden</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈviːsˌbaːdn̩]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden.ogg" title="File:Wiesbaden.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/Wiesbaden.ogg" title="Wiesbaden.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is a city in central western <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and the capital of the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">federal state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>. In July 2016, it had about 288,000 inhabitants, plus approximately 19,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> United States citizens (mostly associated with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>). The Wiesbaden urban area is home to approx. 560,000 people.</p>
<p>The city, together with nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt am Main</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, is part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine_Main_Region" title="Frankfurt Rhine Main Region">Frankfurt Rhine Main Region</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> with a combined population of about 5.8 million people.</p>
<p>Wiesbaden is one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Spa_town" title="Spa town">spa towns</a> in Europe. Its name translates to "meadow baths", making reference to the hot springs. It is internationally famous for its architecture, climate (also called the "Nice of the North"), and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_springs" title="Hot springs">hot springs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> At one time, Wiesbaden boasted 26 hot springs. Fourteen of the springs are still flowing today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1970, the town hosted the tenth <i><a href="/wiki/Hessentag" title="Hessentag">Hessentag</a></i> state festival.</p>
<p>The city is considered the tenth richest in Germany (2014) with 113.3% of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="This sentence is hard to interpret. (April 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Every citizen has an average annual buying power of €24,798.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_setting">Geographical setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geographical setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="958" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/220px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/330px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/440px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite view of Wiesbaden (north of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhine_river" title="Rhine river">Rhine river</a>) and Mainz</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wiesbaden is situated on the right (northern) bank of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> River, below the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a>, where the Rhine's main direction changes from north to west. The city is across the Rhine from Mainz, the capital of the federal state of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>. Frankfurt am Main is located about 38 kilometres (23.6 mi) east. To the north of the city are the <a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus</a> Mountains, which trend in a northeasterly direction.</p>
<p>The city center, the <i>Stadtmitte</i>, is located in the north-easternmost part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Rhine_Valley" title="Upper Rhine Valley">Upper Rhine Valley</a> at the spurs of the <a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus</a> mountains, about 5 kilometres (3.1 mi) from the Rhine. The landscape is formed by a wide lowland between the Taunus heights in the north, the Bierstadter Höhe and the Hainerberg in the east, the Mosbacher Mountain in the south, and the Schiersteiner Mountain in the west, an offshoot of the Taunus range. The downtown is drained only by the narrow valley of the Salzbach, a tributary of the Rhine, on the eastern flanks of the Mosbacher Mountain. The city's main railway line and the Mainz road (<i>Mainzer Straße</i>) follow this valley. Several other streams drain into the Salzbach within the city center: the Wellritzbach, the Kesselbach, the Schwarzbach, the Dambach, and the Tennelbach, as well as the outflow of many thermal and mineral springs in the <i>Kurhaus</i> (spa) district. Above the city center, the Salzbach is better known as the Rambach.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:297px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1274" data-file-width="2596" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg/295px-Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg/443px-Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg/590px-Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg 2x" width="295"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_De_Merian_Hassiae.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Wiesbaden from the <i>Topographia Hassiae</i> by <a href="/wiki/Matth%C3%A4us_Merian" title="Matthäus Merian">Matthäus Merian</a> in 1655.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The highest point of the Wiesbaden municipality is located northwest of the city center near the summit of the Hohe Wurzel, with an elevation of 608 metres (1,995 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. The lowest point is the harbour entrance of Schierstein at 83 metres (272 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. The central square (the <i>Schlossplatz</i>, or palace square) is at an elevation of 115 metres (377 ft).</p>
<p>Wiesbaden covers an area of 204 km<sup>2</sup> (79 sq mi). It is 17.6 kilometres (10.9 mi) from north to south and 19.7 kilometres (12.2 mi) from west to east. In the north are vast forest areas, which cover 27.4% of the urban area. In the west and east are vineyards and agricultural land, which cover 31.1% of the area. Of the municipality's 79 kilometres (49.1 mi)-long border, the Rhine makes up 10.3 kilometres (6.4 mi).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wiesbaden has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperateness" title="Temperateness">temperate</a>-<a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: Cfb) with relatively cold winters and warm summers. Its average annual temperature is 9.8 °C (49.6 °F), with monthly mean temperatures ranging from 1.0 °C (33.8 °F) in January to 18.6 °C (65.5 °F) in July.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2496" data-file-width="1664" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg/175px-Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg/263px-Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg/350px-Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg 2x" width="175"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heidenmauer_in_Wiesbaden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Heidenmauer</i> ("Heathen Wall") of <i>Aquae Mattiacorum</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_antiquity">Classical antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Classical antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While evidence of settlement at present-day Wiesbaden dates back to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> era, historical records document continuous occupancy after the erection of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_empire" title="Roman empire">Roman</a> fort in 6 AD which housed an auxiliary cavalry unit. The <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">thermal springs</a> of Wiesbaden are first mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturalis_Historia" title="Naturalis Historia">Naturalis Historia</a></i>. They were famous for their recreation pools for Roman army horses and possibly as the source of a mineral used for red hair dye (which was very fashionable around the turn of BC/AD among women in Rome).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Roman settlement is first mentioned using the name <i>Aquae Mattiacorum</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "Waters of the Mattiaci") in 121. The <a href="/wiki/Mattiaci" title="Mattiaci">Mattiaci</a> were a <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribe</a>, possibly a branch of the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Chatti" title="Chatti">Chatti</a>, who lived in the vicinity at that time. The town also appears as Mattiacum in <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographia" title="Geographia">Geographia</a> (2.10). The line of Roman frontier fortifications, the <a href="/wiki/Limes_Germanicus" title="Limes Germanicus">Limes Germanicus</a>, was constructed in the <a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus</a> not far north of Wiesbaden.</p>
<p>The capital of the province of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Germania Superior</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mogontiacum" title="Mogontiacum">Mogontiacum</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>), base of 2 (at times 3) Roman legions, was just over the Rhine and connected by a bridge at the present-day borough of <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kastel" title="Mainz-Kastel">Mainz-Kastel</a> (Roman "<i>castellum</i>"), a strongly fortified bridgehead.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alamanni" title="Alamanni">Alamanni</a>, a coalition of Germanic tribes from beyond the <i>Limes</i>, captured the fort around 260. Later, in the 370s, when the Romans and Alamanni were allied, the Alemanni gained control of the Wiesbaden area and were in charge of its defense against other Germanic tribes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> under <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis I</a> defeated the Alamanni in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tolbiac" title="Battle of Tolbiac">Battle of Tolbiac</a> in 496, the Franks eventually displaced the Alamanni in the Wiesbaden area over the course of the 6th century. In the 8th century, Wiesbaden became the site of a royal <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palace</a> of the Frankish kingdom. The first documented use of the name Wiesbaden is by <a href="/wiki/Einhard" title="Einhard">Einhard</a>, the biographer of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, whose writings mention "Wisabada" sometime between 828 and 830.</p>
<p>When the Frankish <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a> broke up in 888, Wiesbaden was in the eastern half, called <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a> (which would evolve into the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>). The town was part of <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a>, the heartland of East Francia. In the 1170s, the <a href="/wiki/Count" title="Count">Count</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nassau_(state)" title="Nassau (state)">Nassau</a>, Walram I, received the area around Wiesbaden as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiefdom" title="Fiefdom">fiefdom</a>. When Franconia fragmented in the early 13th century, Nassau emerged as an independent state as part of the Holy Roman Empire.</p>
<p>In 1232 Wiesbaden became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reichsstadt" title="Reichsstadt">Reichsstadt</a>, an imperial city, of the Holy Roman Empire. However, in 1242, during the war of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a> against the Pope, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Mainz" title="Archbishopric of Mainz">Archbishop of Mainz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siegfried_III_(Archbishop_of_Mainz)" title="Siegfried III (Archbishop of Mainz)">Siegfried III</a>, ordered the city's destruction.</p>
<p>Wiesbaden returned to the control of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Nassau" title="House of Nassau">House of Nassau</a> in 1270 under Count <a href="/wiki/Walram_II,_Count_of_Nassau" title="Walram II, Count of Nassau">Walram II, Count of Nassau</a>. However, Wiesbaden and the castle at <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden-Sonnenberg" title="Wiesbaden-Sonnenberg">Sonnenberg</a> were again destroyed in 1283 in conflict with <a href="/wiki/Eppstein" title="Eppstein">Eppstein</a>.</p>
<p>Walram's son and successor <a href="/wiki/Adolf_of_Germany" title="Adolf of Germany">Adolf</a> would later become king of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Germany" title="Kingdom of Germany">Germany</a> from 1292 until 1298. In 1329, under Adolf's son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerlach_I_of_Nassau-Wiesbaden" title="Gerlach I of Nassau-Wiesbaden">Gerlach I of Nassau-Weilburg</a> the House of Nassau and thereby, Wiesbaden, received the right of <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">coinage</a> from Holy Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Louis IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Louis the Bavarian</a>.</p>
<p>In 1355, the County of Nassau-Weilburg was divided among the sons of Gerlach. The County of Nassau's holdings would be subdivided many times among heirs, with the parts being brought together again whenever a line died out. Wiesbaden became the seat of the County of Nassau-Wiesbaden under Count Adolf I (1307–1370), eldest son of Gerlach. It would eventually fell back to Nassau-Weilburg in 1605.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to its participation in the uprisings of the <a href="/wiki/German_Peasants%27_War" title="German Peasants' War">German Peasants' War</a> of 1525, Wiesbaden lost all its privileges for over 40 years. During this time, Wiesbaden became <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> with the nomination of Wolf Denthener as first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a> pastor on January 1, 1543. The same day, the first <a href="/wiki/Latin_school" title="Latin school">Latin school</a> was opened, preparing pupils for the <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Idstein" title="Idstein">Idstein</a>. In 1566, the privileges of the city were restored.</p>
<p>The oldest remaining building of Wiesbaden, the old city hall, was built in 1609 and 1610. No older buildings are preserved due to two fires in 1547 and 1561. In 1648, at the end of the devastating <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, chronicles tell that Wiesbaden had barely 40 residents left. In 1659, the County of Nassau-Weilburg was divided again. Wiesbaden became part of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=County_of_Nassau-Usingen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="County of Nassau-Usingen (page does not exist)">County of Nassau-Usingen</a>. In 1744, the seat of Nassau-Usingen was moved to <a href="/wiki/Biebrich_(Wiesbaden)" title="Biebrich (Wiesbaden)">Biebrich</a>. In 1771, the Count of Nassau-Usingen granted a concession for gambling in Wiesbaden. In 1810, the Wiesbaden Casino (German: <i>Spielbank</i>) was opened in the old Kurhaus. Gambling was later outlawed by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a> authorities in 1872.</p>
<p>As a result of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s victory over <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Austerlitz" title="Battle of Austerlitz">Battle of Austerlitz</a>, the Holy Roman Empire was dissolved in 1805. On July 12, 1806, 16 states in present-day Germany, including the remaining counties of Nassau-Usingen and Nassau-Weilburg, formally left the Holy Roman Empire and joined together in the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a>. Napoleon was its "protector". Under pressure from Napoleon, both counties merged to form the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Nassau" title="Duchy of Nassau">Duchy of Nassau</a> on August 30, 1806.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg/220px-Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg/330px-Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg/440px-Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Waterloo_Memorian.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Memorial for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nassau_(state)" title="Nassau (state)">Nassauers</a> fallen at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the 1815 <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, the Duchy of Nassau joined the <a href="/wiki/German_Confederation" title="German Confederation">German Confederation</a>. The capital of Nassau was moved from Weilburg to Wiesbaden, and the city became the ducal residence. Building activity started to give the city a magnificent appearance. Most of the historical center of Wiesbaden dates back to this time.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1920" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg/220px-Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg/330px-Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg/440px-Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Innenstadt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Marktkirche,_Wiesbaden" title="Marktkirche, Wiesbaden">Marktkirche</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Boos" title="Carl Boos">Carl Boos</a>: Its neo-Gothic steeple dominates the <a href="/wiki/Pentagon_(Wiesbaden)" title="Pentagon (Wiesbaden)">Historical Pentagon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, 30,000 citizens of Nassau assembled in Wiesbaden on March 4. They demanded a constitution from the Duke, which they received.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War" title="Austro-Prussian War">Austro-Prussian War</a> of 1866, Nassau took Austria's side. This decision led to the end of the duchy. After the Austrian defeat, Nassau was annexed by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> and became part of the Prussian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Hesse-Nassau" title="Province of Hesse-Nassau">province of Hesse-Nassau</a>. The deposed duke <a href="/wiki/Adolphe,_Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" title="Adolphe, Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Adolph of Nassau</a> in 1890 became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" title="Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Grand Duke of Luxembourg</a> (see <a href="/wiki/House_of_Nassau" title="House of Nassau">House of Nassau</a>). This turned out to be a fortunate change for the city, as it then became an international spa town. A rise in construction commenced after the aristocracy followed the lead of the Hohenzollern emperors, who began annual trips to Wiesbaden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The period around the turn of the 20th century is regarded as the heyday of the city. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_II" title="Kaiser Wilhelm II">Kaiser Wilhelm II</a> visited the city regularly in summer, such that it became an unofficial "summer residence". The city was also popular among the Russian nobility. In the wake of the imperial court, numerous nobles, artists, and wealthy businessmen increasingly settled in the city. Many wealthy persons chose Wiesbaden as their retirement seat, as it offered leisure and medical treatment alike. In the latter part of the 19th century, Wiesbaden became the German city with the most millionaires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1894, the present Hessian State Theater, designed by the Vienna architects Fellner and Helmer, was built on behalf of Kaiser Wilhelm II.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weimar_Republic_and_Third_Reich_.281919_to_1945.29">Weimar Republic and Third Reich (1919 to 1945)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Weimar Republic and Third Reich (1919 to 1945)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After World War I, Wiesbaden fell under the Allied occupation of the Rhineland and was occupied by the French army in 1918. In 1921, the Wiesbaden Agreement on German reparations to France was signed in the city. In 1925, Wiesbaden became the headquarters of the British Rhine Army until the withdrawal of occupying forces from the Rhineland in 1930.</p>
<p>In 1929, an airport was constructed in Erbenheim on the site of a horse-racing track. In 1936, Fighter Squadron 53 of the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> was stationed here.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a> pogrom on November 10, 1938, Wiesbaden's large synagogue on Michelsberg was destroyed. The synagogue had been designed by Phillip Hoffmann and built in 1869. Another synagogue in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiesbaden-Bierstadt" title="Wiesbaden-Bierstadt">Wiesbaden-Bierstadt</a> was also destroyed. When the Nazis came to power in Germany, there were 2,700 Jews living in Wiesbaden. By June 1942 nearly all of them had been deported to the death camps in Poland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>General <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Beck" title="Ludwig Beck">Ludwig Beck</a> from Wiesbaden was one of the planners of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/July_20_plot" title="July 20 plot">July 20, 1944 assassination attempt</a> of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. Beck was designated by his fellow conspirators to be future Head of State (Regent) after elimination of Hitler. The plot failed, however, and Beck was forced to commit suicide. Today, the city annually awards the Ludwig Beck prize for civil courage in his honor.</p>
<p>Lutheran pastor and theologian <a href="/wiki/Martin_Niem%C3%B6ller" title="Martin Niemöller">Martin Niemöller</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Confessing_Church" title="Confessing Church">Confessing Church</a> resistance movement against the Nazis, is an Honorary Citizen of Wiesbaden. He presented his last sermon before his arrest in Wiesbaden's Market Church.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In World War II, Wiesbaden was the Headquarters for Germany’s <a href="/wiki/Military_district_(Germany)" title="Military district (Germany)">Wehrkreis XII</a>. This military district included the <a href="/wiki/Eifel" title="Eifel">Eifel</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_(region)" title="Palatinate (region)">Palatinate</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a>, this <i>Wehrkreis</i> was extended to include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" title="Lorraine (region)">Lorraine</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Nancy,_France" title="Nancy, France">Nancy</a>, and the Grand Duchy of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>. The commander was <i>General der Infanterie</i> <a href="/wiki/Walther_Schroth" title="Walther Schroth">Walther Schroth</a>.</p>
<p><i>Wehrkreis</i> XII was made up of three subordinate regions: <i>Bereich Hauptsitze</i> <a href="/wiki/Koblenz" title="Koblenz">Koblenz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Bereich Hauptsitz</i> Koblenz was the headquarters for 12 <i>Unterregion-Hauptsitze</i>, namely <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">Trier</a> I, Trier II, <a href="/wiki/Koblenz" title="Koblenz">Koblenz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuwied" title="Neuwied">Neuwied</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kreuznach" title="Kreuznach">Kreuznach</a>, Wiesbaden, <a href="/wiki/Limburg_an_der_Lahn" title="Limburg an der Lahn">Limburg an der Lahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lahn" title="Lahn">Lahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.</li>
<li><i>Bereich Hauptsitz</i> Mannheim was the headquarters for 10 <i>Unterregion-Hauptsitze</i>, namely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saarlautern" title="Saarlautern">Saarlautern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken" title="Saarbrücken">Saarbrücken</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Wendel" title="St. Wendel">St. Wendel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zweibr%C3%BCcken" title="Zweibrücken">Zweibrücken</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaiserslautern" title="Kaiserslautern">Kaiserslautern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neustadt_an_der_Weinstra%C3%9Fe" title="Neustadt an der Weinstraße">Neustadt an der Weinstraße</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwigshafen" title="Ludwigshafen">Ludwigshafen</a> (Rhein), <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a> I, Mannheim II and <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg" title="Heidelberg">Heidelberg</a>.</li>
<li><i>Bereich Hauptsitz</i> Metz was the headquarters for <i>Unterregion-Hauptsitze</i> <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diedenhofen" title="Diedenhofen">Diedenhofen</a> (Thionville) and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Avold" title="Saint-Avold">Saint-Avold</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>During the war, Wiesbaden was largely spared by allied bombing raids. But between August 1940 and March 1945, Wiesbaden was attacked by Allied bombers on 66 days. In the attacks, about 18% of the city's homes were destroyed. During the war, more than 25% of the city's buildings were damaged or worse and 1,700 people were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinrich-Verlag_GmBH_2011_80_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heinrich-Verlag_GmBH_2011_80-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Wiesbaden was captured by U.S. Army forces on March 28, 1945. The U.S. 317th Infantry Regiment attacked in assault boats across the Rhine from Mainz while the 319th Infantry attacked across the Main River near <a href="/wiki/Hochheim_am_Main" title="Hochheim am Main">Hochheim am Main</a>. The attack started at 0100 and by early afternoon the two forces of the <a href="/wiki/80th_Division_(United_States)" title="80th Division (United States)">80th U.S. Infantry Division</a> had linked up with the loss of only three dead and three missing. The Americans captured 900 German soldiers and a warehouse full of 4,000 cases of champagne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the war's end, American pop artist <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> was stationed in Friedberg and often visited Wiesbaden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heinrich-Verlag_GmBH_2011_80_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heinrich-Verlag_GmBH_2011_80-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_and_contemporary_history">Cold War and contemporary history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cold War and contemporary history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After World War II, the state of Hesse was established (see <a href="/wiki/Greater_Hesse" title="Greater Hesse">Greater Hesse</a>), and Wiesbaden became its capital, though nearby <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt am Main</a> is much larger and contains many Hessian government offices. Wiesbaden however suffered much less than Frankfurt from air bombing. There is a persistent rumour that the U.S. Army Air Force spared the town with the intention of turning it into a postwar HQ, but USAAF sources claim this to be a myth, arguing that Wiesbaden's economic and strategic importance simply did not justify more bombing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Wiesbaden was host to the Headquarters, U.S. Air Forces, Europe based at the former <a href="/wiki/Europaviertel_(Wiesbaden)" title="Europaviertel (Wiesbaden)">Lindsey Air Station</a> from 1953 to 1973.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_armed_forces" title="American armed forces">American armed forces</a> have been present in Wiesbaden since World War II. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._1st_Armored_Division" title="U.S. 1st Armored Division">U.S. 1st Armored Division</a> was headquartered at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiesbaden_Army_Airfield" title="Wiesbaden Army Airfield">Wiesbaden Army Airfield</a>, just off the <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> toward Frankfurt, until the Division completed relocation to Fort Bliss, Texas in 2011. Wiesbaden is now home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Europe" title="U.S. Army Europe">U.S. Army Europe</a> Headquarters and Mission Command Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bathing_and_gambling">Bathing and gambling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Bathing and gambling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Wiesbaden has long been famous for its thermal springs and spa. Use of the thermal springs was first documented by the Romans. The business of spring bathing became important for Wiesbaden near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. By 1370, 16 bath houses were in operation. By 1800, the city had 2,239 inhabitants and 23 bath houses. By 1900, Wiesbaden, with a population of 86,100, hosted 126,000 visitors annually. Famous visitors to the springs included <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann Wolfgang von Goethe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoevsky">Fyodor Dostoevsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Pontoppidan" title="Henrik Pontoppidan">Henrik Pontoppidan</a>. In those years, more millionaires were living in Wiesbaden than in any other city in Germany.</p>
<p>Gambling followed bathing <i>en suite</i>, and in the 19th century, Wiesbaden was famous for both. Its casino (<i>Spielbank</i>) rivalled those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg" title="Bad Homburg">Bad Homburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baden-Baden" title="Baden-Baden">Baden-Baden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>. In 1872, the Prussian-dominated imperial government closed down all German gambling houses. The Wiesbaden casino was reopened in 1949.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1288px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg" title="Panorama of Wiesbaden from the Neroberg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="6347" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg/1280px-MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg/1920px-MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg/2560px-MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg 2x" width="1280"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MK_36878-82_Wiesbaden_vom_Neroberg.jpg" title="File:MK 36878-82 Wiesbaden vom Neroberg.jpg"></a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Palace_Square">The Palace Square</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The Palace Square">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1394" data-file-width="1920" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg/225px-Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg/338px-Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg/450px-Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stadtschloss_Wiesbaden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Former Ducal Palace</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Schlo%C3%9Fplatz_(Wiesbaden)" title="Schloßplatz (Wiesbaden)">Schloßplatz</a></i> ("palace square") is situated in the center of the city, surrounded by several outstanding buildings. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stadtschloss,_Wiesbaden" title="Stadtschloss, Wiesbaden">ducal palace</a> was begun under <a href="/wiki/William,_Duke_of_Nassau" title="William, Duke of Nassau">William, Duke of Nassau</a>. Its foundations were laid in 1837 and it was completed in November 1841 (two years after William's death). For the twenty-six remaining years of ducal authority it was the residence of the ruling family. It later served as a secondary residence for the King of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> 1866 to 1918. It was later used as a headquarters for French and British occupying forces after World War I, then as a museum. Since 1945, the building has served as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hessian_Landtag" title="Hessian Landtag">Landtag</a> (parliamentary building) for the federal state of Hesse. The site of the palace had been that of a castle, probably from the early Middle Ages, around which the city had developed. While nothing is known of the former castle, remains of it were uncovered during excavations after World War II.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden,_1893.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2588" data-file-width="3860" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden%2C_1893.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Altes_Rathaus_-_Wiesbaden,_1893.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New Town Hall, picture taken 1893</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1693" data-file-width="2539" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg/220px-MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg/330px-MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg/440px-MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MK10960_Marktstra%C3%9Fe_16_Altes_Rathaus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old Town Hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The new town hall was built in 1887. Engraved in the paving in front of the town hall are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heraldic_beast" title="Heraldic beast">heraldic eagle</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, the lion of Nassau, and the <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">fleur-de-lis</a> of Wiesbaden. The old town hall, built in 1610, is the oldest preserved building in the city center and now is used as a civil registry office.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Marktkirche,_Wiesbaden" title="Marktkirche, Wiesbaden">Marktkirche</a></i> ("market church") was built from 1852 to 1862 in a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">neo-Gothic</a> style. Its western steeple is 92 m (302 ft) in height, making the church the highest building in the city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kurhaus_and_Theater">Kurhaus and Theater</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Kurhaus and Theater">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1078" data-file-width="1616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg/220px-Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg/330px-Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg/440px-Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kurhaus_Wiesbaden_blaue_Stunde_290-L4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kurhaus with Fontain on the Bowling Green</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kurhaus,_Wiesbaden" title="Kurhaus, Wiesbaden">Kurhaus, Wiesbaden</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hessisches_Staatstheater_Wiesbaden" title="Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden">Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bowling_Green,_Wiesbaden" title="Bowling Green, Wiesbaden">Bowling Green, Wiesbaden</a></div>
<p>The monumental <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neo-Classical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kurhaus,_Wiesbaden" title="Kurhaus, Wiesbaden">Kurhaus</a></i> ("spa house") was built at the request of Kaiser <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II_of_Germany" title="Wilhelm II of Germany">Wilhelm II</a> between 1904 and 1907. Its famous <i>Spielbank</i> (casino) is again in operation.</p>
<p>In front of the Kurhaus is a lawn known as the Bowling Green. To one side of the Bowling Green is the Kurhaus Kolonnade. Built in 1827, the 129 meter structure is the longest hall in Europe supported by pillars. To the other side is the Theater Kolonnade, built in 1839. It is adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Hessisches_Staatstheater_Wiesbaden" title="Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden">Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden</a>, built between 1892 and 1894.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Bonifatius">St. Bonifatius</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: St. Bonifatius">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/St._Bonifatius,_Wiesbaden" title="St. Bonifatius, Wiesbaden">St. Bonifatius, Wiesbaden</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/St._Bonifatius,_Wiesbaden" title="St. Bonifatius, Wiesbaden">St. Bonifatius</a>, the first church for the Catholic community after the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a>, was built from 1845 until 1849 by Philipp Hoffmann in <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival style</a> and dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Elizabeth.27s_Church">St. Elizabeth's Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: St. Elizabeth's Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Russian Orthodox <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth%27s_Church,_Wiesbaden" title="St. Elizabeth's Church, Wiesbaden">Church of Saint Elizabeth</a> was built on the <a href="/wiki/Neroberg" title="Neroberg">Neroberg</a> from 1847 to 1855 by Duke Adolf of Nassau on the occasion of the early death of his wife <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Mikhailovna" title="Elizabeth Mikhailovna">Elizabeth Mikhailovna</a>, who died in childbirth. The architect was Philipp Hoffmann.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sights">Other sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="5847" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG/220px-Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG/330px-Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG/440px-Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Warmer_Damm_Pond_and_Fountain.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A pond and fountain in the Warmer Damm</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another building from the regency of Duke Wilhelm is the Luisenplatz, a square named for the Duke's first wife. It is surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassicist</a> buildings, and in the middle of the square is the Waterloo <a href="/wiki/Obelisk" title="Obelisk">Obelisk</a>, commemorating the Nassauers who died in the wars against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon</a>. Apart from the palace in the center, the ducal family had a large palace on the banks of the Rhine, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schloss_Biebrich" title="Schloss Biebrich">Schloss Biebrich</a>. This <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">baroque building</a> was erected in the first half of the 18th century.</p>
<p>North of the city is the <a href="/wiki/Neroberg" title="Neroberg">Neroberg</a>. From the top of this hill it is possible to view a panorama of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Nerobergbahn" title="Nerobergbahn">Nerobergbahn</a> <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular railway</a> connects the city with the hill.</p>
<p>One of the three Hessian state museums, <a href="/wiki/Museum_Wiesbaden" title="Museum Wiesbaden">Museum Wiesbaden</a> is located in Wiesbaden.</p>
<p>Other churches are the <a href="/wiki/Bergkirche,_Wiesbaden" title="Bergkirche, Wiesbaden">Bergkirche</a>, completed in 1879 in Gothic Revival style, and the <a href="/wiki/Lutherkirche,_Wiesbaden" title="Lutherkirche, Wiesbaden">Lutherkirche</a>, finished in 1910 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jugendstil" title="Jugendstil">Jugendstil</a>.</p>
<p>The Warme Damm is a 4.5-hectare park on the east side of Wilhelmstrasse and south of the State theater and Kurhaus which features a lake, a fountain, various statues, and large grassy areas. The park was created in 1859–1860 and is named after the medieval fortifications around a pond into which the warm waters of the town's 26 warm springs flowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs_of_Wiesbaden">Boroughs of Wiesbaden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Boroughs of Wiesbaden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city of Wiesbaden is divided into 26 boroughs: five in the central city and 21 suburban districts. The 21 suburban districts were incorporated in four phases from 1926 to 1977. The former right Mainz suburbs Amöneburg, Kastel and Kostheim have belonged to Wiesbaden since 1945.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_subdivisions_(colored_scheme).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1014" data-file-width="1126" height="360" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg/400px-Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg/600px-Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg/800px-Wiesbaden_subdivisions_%28colored_scheme%29.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_subdivisions_(colored_scheme).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Boroughs of Wiesbaden</div>
