<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mayors">Mayors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mayors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1849–1868: Heinrich Fischer</li>
<li>1868–1882: Wilhelm Lanz</li>
<li>1882–1883: Christian Schlichter</li>
<li>1883–1913: Carl Bernhard von Ibell</li>
<li>1913–1919: Karl Glässing</li>
<li>1919–1929: Fritz Travers</li>
<li>1930–1933: Georg Krücke</li>
<li>1933–1937: Alfred Schulte</li>
<li>1937–1945: <a href="/wiki/Erich_Mix" title="Erich Mix">Erich Mix</a></li>
<li>1945–1946: Georg Krücke</li>
<li>1946–1953: Hans Heinrich Redlhammer</li>
<li>1951–1954: Georg Kluge</li>
<li>1954–1960: <a href="/wiki/Erich_Mix" title="Erich Mix">Erich Mix</a></li>
<li>1960–1968: Georg Buch</li>
<li>1968–1980: Rudi Schmitt</li>
<li>1980–1982: Georg-Berndt Oschatz</li>
<li>1982–1985: Hans-Joachim Jentsch</li>
<li>1985–1997: Achim Exner</li>
<li>1997–2007: Hildebrand Diehl</li>
<li>2007–2013: Helmut Müller</li>
<li>2013– <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sven_Gerich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sven Gerich (page does not exist)">Sven Gerich</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The information up to 2007 was retrieved from <i>Die Wiesbadener Oberbürgermeister seit dem Bau des neuen Rathauses (1886)</i> (The Wiesbaden Mayors since the construction of the new town mayor hall (1886).)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1838" data-file-width="2997" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png/220px-Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png/330px-Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png/440px-Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roadmap_Wiesbaden.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Wiesbaden with Autobahns, federal roads and main streets.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wiesbaden is well connected to the German motorway (<i><a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a></i>) system. The <a href="/wiki/Wiesbadener_Kreuz" title="Wiesbadener Kreuz">Wiesbadener Kreuz</a> is an Autobahn interchange eastwards the city where the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">Bundesautobahn 3</a> (A 3), <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> to <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_66" title="Bundesautobahn 66">Bundesautobahn 66</a> (A 66), <a href="/wiki/Rheingau" title="Rheingau">Rheingau</a> to <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a>, meet. With approximately 190,000 cars daily it is one of the most heavily used interchange in Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_66" title="Bundesautobahn 66">Bundesautobahn 66</a> (A 66) connects Wiesbaden with <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_643" title="Bundesautobahn 643">Bundesautobahn 643</a> (A 643) is mainly a commuter motorway which starts in the south of the city centre, runs through the southern part of Wiesbaden crosses the Rhine river via the <a href="/wiki/Schierstein_Bridge" title="Schierstein Bridge">Schierstein Bridge</a> and connect in the northwestern part of <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> to the A60. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_671" title="Bundesautobahn 671">Bundesautobahn 671</a> (A 671) is a very short motorway in the southeastern part of Wiesbaden which primarily serves as a fast connection between the city centre and the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_60" title="Bundesautobahn 60">Bundesautobahn 60</a> to serve the cities like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Neckar" title="Rhine-Neckar">Rhine-Neckar region</a> (Mannheim, Ludwigshafen and Heidelberg).</p>
<p>The downtown area is bordered on the north side by Taunusstrasse, which has once featured many antique stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The east side is constrained by Wilhelmstrasse, created by Christian Zais. This 1,000 meter-long street is named after Archduke Wilhelm, not Emperor Wilhelm II, as many mistakenly believe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The streets of central Wiesbaden are regularly congested with cars during rush hour. Besides some areas, especially the <a href="/wiki/Ringstra%C3%9Fe_(Wiesbaden)" title="Ringstraße (Wiesbaden)">Ringroad</a> and not directly in the centre, and the southern arterial roads like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainzer_Stra%C3%9Fe" title="Mainzer Straße">Mainzer Straße</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biebricher_Allee" title="Biebricher Allee">Biebricher Allee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schiersteiner_Stra%C3%9Fe" title="Schiersteiner Straße">Schiersteiner Straße</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg/220px-BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg/330px-BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg/440px-BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BD-HauptbahnhofWiesbaden-20130507-IMG_1754.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden_Hauptbahnhof" title="Wiesbaden Hauptbahnhof">Wiesbaden main station</a>, built between 1904 and 1906.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden_Hauptbahnhof" title="Wiesbaden Hauptbahnhof">Wiesbaden's main railway station</a> and several minor railway stops connect the town with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Central_Station" title="Frankfurt Central Station">Frankfurt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Darmstadt_Central_Station" title="Darmstadt Central Station">Darmstadt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainz_Central_Station" title="Mainz Central Station">Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limburg_(Lahn)_station" title="Limburg (Lahn) station">Limburg</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koblenz_Central_Station" title="Koblenz Central Station">Koblenz</a> via <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=R%C3%BCdesheim_station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rüdesheim station (page does not exist)">Rüdesheim</a>. Wiesbaden Hauptbahnhof is connected to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cologne-Frankfurt_high-speed_rail_line" title="Cologne-Frankfurt high-speed rail line">Cologne-Frankfurt high-speed rail line</a> by a 13-kilometer <a href="/wiki/Breckenheim%E2%80%93Wiesbaden_railway" title="Breckenheim–Wiesbaden railway">branch line</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamburg_Central_Station" title="Hamburg Central Station">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="München Hauptbahnhof">München</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leipzig_Central_Station" title="Leipzig Central Station">Leipzig</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dresden_Central_Station" title="Dresden Central Station">Dresden</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stuttgart_Central_Station" title="Stuttgart Central Station">Stuttgart</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mannheim_Central_Station" title="Mannheim Central Station">Mannheim</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanover_Central_Station" title="Hanover Central Station">Hanover</a> are connected directly to Wiesbaden via long distance service of the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>. More services to locations outside the immediate area connect through Mainz or <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">Frankfurt Airport</a> or Frankfurt Hauptbahnhof. Regional trains and bus services are coordinated by the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund" title="Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund">Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg/220px-Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg/330px-Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg/440px-Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Citaro_G_II_ESWE.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Bus at Schierstein harbor</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b>S-Bahn</b></li>
</ul>
<p>Wiesbaden is connected to the Frankfurt <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S-Bahn_Rhein-Main" title="S-Bahn Rhein-Main">S-Bahn</a> network and served by three lines (S1, S8 and S9) which connect Wiesbaden with the densely populated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhein-Main_Region" title="Frankfurt Rhein-Main Region">Rhine Main Region</a>. All routes have an at least 30 minute service during the day, in the rush hour partially every 15 minutes schedule. It provides access to nearby cities such as <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim" title="Rüsselsheim">Rüsselsheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanau" title="Hanau">Hanau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Offenbach_am_Main" title="Offenbach am Main">Offenbach am Main</a> and smaller towns that are on the way.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Bus</b></li>
</ul>
<p>The city's public transportation service <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESWE_Verkehr" title="ESWE Verkehr">ESWE Verkehr</a> connects all city districts to downtown by 45 bus lines in the daytime and 9 bus lines in the night. Five more bus lines, operated by the public transportation service of the city of Mainz, connects Wiesbaden's districts <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kastel" title="Mainz-Kastel">Kastel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kostheim" title="Mainz-Kostheim">Kostheim</a> to Mainz downtown.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1206" data-file-width="1760" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/220px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/330px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg/440px-AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AirportFrankfurt_fromair_2010-09-19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of Frankfurt Airport</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>The city can easily be accessed from around the world via <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> (<i>Flughafen Frankfurt am Main</i>) which is located 15 km (8 mi) east of Wiesbaden. The airport has four <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> and serves 265 non-stop destinations. Run by transport company <a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport</a> it ranks among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's 10 busiest airports by passenger traffic</a> and is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by cargo traffic">second busiest airport by cargo traffic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. The airport also serves as a hub for <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> and as the main hub for German <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>. Depending on whether total passengers or flights are used, it ranks second or third busiest in Europe alongside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris Charles de Gaulle Airport</a>. Passenger traffic at Frankfurt Airport in 2011 was 56.5 million.</p>
<p>The airport can be reached by car or train and has two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway_station" title="Railway station">railway stations</a>, one for regional and one for long-distance traffic. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S-Bahn" title="S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> lines S8 and S9 (direction <i>Offenbach Ost</i> or <i>Hanau Hbf</i>) departing at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_Regional_Train_Station" title="Frankfurt Airport Regional Train Station">regional train station</a> take 30 minutes from the airport to Wiesbaden Central Station, the <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> trains departing at the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">long-distance railway station</a> take also 30 minutes to the central station.</p>
<ul>
<li><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Hahn_Airport" title="Frankfurt Hahn Airport">Frankfurt Hahn Airport</a></b></li>
</ul>
<p>Despite the name, Frankfurt Hahn Airport (<i>Flughafen Frankfurt-Hahn</i>) is not located anywhere near Frankfurt but is instead situated approximately 100 km (62 mi) from the city in <a href="/wiki/Lautzenhausen" title="Lautzenhausen">Lautzenhausen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>). Hahn Airport is a major base for <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">Low-cost carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. This airport can be reached by car or bus. The nearest train station is in <a href="/wiki/Traben-Trarbach" title="Traben-Trarbach">Traben-Trarbach</a>, it is ca. 17 km (11 mi) from the airport, on foot. The roads are not lit.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are small container port operations nearby on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> rivers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lucius_D._Clay_Kaserne" title="Lucius D. Clay Kaserne">Lucius D. Clay Kaserne</a> (Formerly Wiesbaden Army Airfield or WAAF) is located adjacent to Wiesbaden-Erbenheim and is home to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Army_Europe" title="US Army Europe">US Army in Europe</a> (USAREUR) headquarters, the 5th Signal Command and the 66th Military Intelligence Brigade. The airfield was one of the points of origin for flights to Berlin in support of Operation Vittles (the Berlin airlift) during the Soviet blockade of Berlin. General Clay, the commander of the US occupation zone in Germany, was the architect of the airlift.</p>
<p>The United States Army runs a garrison in Wiesbaden. The facilities for US soldiers and families are spread across various locations including: Aukamn, Hainerberg, Mainz-Kastel and the Wiesbaden Army-Airfield, where the names of the streets are named after servicemen and women who sacrificed their lives during the Berlin Airlift.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Wiesbaden hosts a number of international companies, which have their German or European headquarters here, for example, <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Laboratories" title="Abbott Laboratories">Abbott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_Sciences_Corporation" title="Computer Sciences Corporation">CSC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal-Mogul" title="Federal-Mogul">Federal-Mogul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_IT" title="Melbourne IT">Melbourne IT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Cruise_Line" title="Norwegian Cruise Line">Norwegian Cruise Line</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Svenska_Cellulosa_Aktiebolaget" title="Svenska Cellulosa Aktiebolaget">SCA</a>. Several German companies also have their headquarters in Wiesbaden, including <a href="/wiki/SGL_Carbon" title="SGL Carbon">SGL Carbon</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Dyckerhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dyckerhoff (page does not exist)">Dyckerhoff</a>, <a href="/wiki/KION_Group" title="KION Group">Kion</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=DBV-Winterthur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="DBV-Winterthur (page does not exist)">DBV-Winterthur</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=R_%2B_V_Versicherung&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="R + V Versicherung (page does not exist)">R + V Versicherung</a>. Wiesbaden is also home to the "Industriepark Kalle-Albert", an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_park" title="Industrial park">industrial park</a> in the southern quarter of <a href="/wiki/Biebrich_(Wiesbaden)" title="Biebrich (Wiesbaden)">Biebrich</a>. It is one of the largest in Germany with over 80 companies from the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry" title="Pharmaceutical industry">pharmaceutical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical</a> industry, including <a href="/wiki/Agfa-Gevaert" title="Agfa-Gevaert">Agfa-Gevaert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clariant" title="Clariant">Clariant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Chemical_Corporation" title="Mitsubishi Chemical Corporation">Mitsubishi Chemical Corporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shin-Etsu_Chemical" title="Shin-Etsu Chemical">Shin-Etsu Chemical</a>. The park was founded by chemical company <a href="/wiki/Hoechst_AG" title="Hoechst AG">Hoechst AG</a> in 1997.</p>
<p>In addition, a large number of Hessian ministries are located in Wiesbaden.</p>
<p>At approximately €77,500, Wiesbaden has the second largest gross domestic product per inhabitant in Hesse, after Frankfurt, making it one of the richest cities in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The purchasing power per inhabitant is €22,500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kaufkraft-Kennziffern_.28IHK_Wiesbaden.29_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kaufkraft-Kennziffern_.28IHK_Wiesbaden.29-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_May_Festival">International May Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: International May Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Internationale_Maifestspiele_Wiesbaden" title="Internationale Maifestspiele Wiesbaden">Internationale Maifestspiele Wiesbaden</a></div>
<p>The International May Festival is an annual arts festival presented by the <a href="/wiki/Hessisches_Staatstheater_Wiesbaden" title="Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden">Hessisches Staatstheater Wiesbaden</a> every May. Established in 1896, it is one of the most distinguished international theatre and music festivals in the world. The festival features performances of plays, musicals, operas, and ballets. Concerts from a wide array of music are featured, as are artistic circus acts and modern dance presentations. Lectures, recitals, cabaret performances, and readings are also featured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rheingau_Wine_Festival">Rheingau Wine Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Rheingau Wine Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The wines and sparkling wines of the close <a href="/wiki/Rheingau" title="Rheingau">Rheingau</a> are presented annually at the ten-day festival in August, <i>Rheingauer Weinwoche</i> (Rheingau Wine Week) around the Wiesbaden City Hall, on the Schlossplatz (Palace Square), the square <i>Dern’sches Gelände</i> and in the pedestrian area. At 118 booths, Rheingau and Wiesbaden vintners offer their wine and sparkling wine and invite to discover the already well known and favored, but also new vintages. Every year thousands of visitors use this opportunity to get acquainted with Rheingau Riesling wines and all their various facets and flavors. Regional specialities compatible with the wines are offered as well. A diversified musical program entertains the wine festival guests. Initiated more than 30 years ago by the Rheingau vintners, this wine festival has a long tradition.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_Star_Market">Shooting Star Market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Shooting Star Market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Wiesbaden’s Sternschnuppenmarkt is located at the central <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden#Main_sights" title="Wiesbaden">Schlossplatz</a> and the neighbouring streets of the <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden#Main_sights" title="Wiesbaden">parliamentary building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden#Main_sights" title="Wiesbaden">old town hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden#Main_sights" title="Wiesbaden">market church</a>. The Sternschnuppenmarkt takes place from the end of November until December 23 every year and is open from Monday until Thursday 10:30 – 9:00 pm, Friday and Saturday 10:30 – 9:30 pm, and Sunday 12:00 – 9:00 pm.</p>
<p>The market is related to the city arms of Wiesbaden: the colours blue and gold and the three lilies are characteristic. Four gates and an illuminated floral roof symbolizing <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">Fleur-de-lis</a>, consisting of twelve over ten metre high and twelve metre wide luminous lilies, emboss the Sternschnuppenmarkt.</p>
<p>Over 110 booths are decorated in oriental style, coloured blue and gold, offering Christmas style goods, arts and crafts as well as nostalgic carousels and a toy train. A Christmas tree more than 28 metres tall is decorated with 1000 blue and golden ties, 2500 electric bulbs and 30 flash bulbs. The nativity scene displays life-sized wooden figures.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rheingau_Musik_Festival">Rheingau Musik Festival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rheingau Musik Festival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the beginning in 1988 the <a href="/wiki/Rheingau_Musik_Festival" title="Rheingau Musik Festival">Rheingau Musik Festival</a> has staged summer concerts in the <a href="/wiki/Marktkirche,_Wiesbaden" title="Marktkirche, Wiesbaden">Marktkirche</a> and in the concert hall of the <a href="/wiki/Kurhaus,_Wiesbaden" title="Kurhaus, Wiesbaden">Kurhaus</a> now named Friedrich-von-Thiersch-Saal.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="877" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg/225px-Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg/338px-Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg/450px-Wiesbaden_Pedestrian.jpg 2x" width="225"/></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since 2007 Wiesbaden has been home to <a href="/wiki/SV_Wehen_Wiesbaden" title="SV Wehen Wiesbaden">SV Wehen Wiesbaden</a>, an association football team that formerly played in nearby <a href="/wiki/Taunusstein" title="Taunusstein">Taunusstein</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Wiesbaden maintains official partnerships with 14 cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wiesbadensistercities_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wiesbadensistercities-49">[49]</a></sup> Town twinnings between Wiesbaden and other cities began with Klagenfurt in 1930, one of the first town-twinnings in Germany.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Wiesbaden's <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> features <a href="/wiki/Fleur-de-lis" title="Fleur-de-lis">fleurs-de-lys</a>, stylized representations of the city's heraldic symbol, the lily. The <a href="/wiki/Blazon" title="Blazon">blazon</a> is: "Azure, two and one fleurs-de-lys Or".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Notable people born in Wiesbaden include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adolphus_Busch" title="Adolphus Busch">Adolphus Busch</a> - founder of <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a>, the year he was born his birthplace belonged to the city of Mainz not Wiesbaden (born in <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kastel" title="Mainz-Kastel">Mainz-Kastel</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarah_Colonna" title="Sarah Colonna">Sarah Colonna</a> - comedian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Grabowski" title="Jürgen Grabowski">Jürgen Grabowski</a> (born 1944), Footballer who played for <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Hanenberger" title="Peter Hanenberger">Peter Hanenberger</a> - automotive specialist for <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>, previously chairman for Australian car giant, <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Kessler" title="Michael Kessler">Michael Kessler</a> - German comedian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shy_Love" title="Shy Love">Shy Love</a> - American pornographic actress.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCnther_L%C3%BCtjens" title="Günther Lütjens">Günther Lütjens</a> - admiral and commander of the World War II naval <a href="/wiki/Operation_Rhein%C3%BCbung" title="Operation Rheinübung">Operation Rheinübung</a>, aboard the battleship <a href="/wiki/German_battleship_Bismarck" title="German battleship Bismarck"><i>Bismarck</i></a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a> - American tennis star (born on a U.S. military base at Wiesbaden).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Melody_Perkins" title="Melody Perkins">Melody Perkins</a> - actress who played in <i><a href="/wiki/Power_Rangers_in_Space" title="Power Rangers in Space">Power Rangers in Space</a></i>, and in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_Rangers:_Lost_Galaxy" title="Power Rangers: Lost Galaxy">Power Rangers: Lost Galaxy</a></i> as the new pink ranger.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bud_Pierce" title="Bud Pierce">Bud Pierce</a> (born 1956) - American politician.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dieter_Rams" title="Dieter Rams">Dieter Rams</a> - former head of design for <a href="/wiki/Braun_(company)" title="Braun (company)">Braun</a>.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rudolf_von_Ribbentrop" title="Rudolf von Ribbentrop">Rudolf von Ribbentrop</a> (born 1921) - captain in the <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">Waffen-SS</a>, recipient of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knights_Cross_of_the_Iron_Cross" title="Knights Cross of the Iron Cross">Knights Cross of the Iron Cross</a> for bravery, son of German foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Joachim_von_Ribbentrop" title="Joachim von Ribbentrop">Joachim von Ribbentrop</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nico_Rosberg" title="Nico Rosberg">Nico Rosberg</a> - 2016 <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> <a href="/wiki/2016_Formula_One_season" title="2016 Formula One season">World Champion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Volker_Schl%C3%B6ndorff" title="Volker Schlöndorff">Volker Schlöndorff</a> - (born 1939), German film director.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Schwarzschild" title="Henry Schwarzschild">Henry Schwarzschild</a> - founder of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCADP" title="NCADP">NCADP</a>, LCDC, and head of ACLU's Capital Punishment project in America.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kiki_Vandeweghe" title="Kiki Vandeweghe">Kiki Vandeweghe</a> - two-time <a href="/wiki/List_of_NBA_All-Stars" title="List of NBA All-Stars">NBA All-Star</a> player, later a general manager and coach.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Valerie_Weigmann" title="Valerie Weigmann">Valerie Weigmann</a> - actress, host and <a href="/wiki/Miss_World_Philippines_2014" title="Miss World Philippines 2014">Miss World Philippines 2014</a> titleholder.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maria_Yakunchikova" title="Maria Yakunchikova">Maria Vasilievna Yakunchikova-Weber</a> - painter.</li>
</ul>
<p>Others who have resided in Wiesbaden include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Carl_Faberg%C3%A9" title="Peter Carl Fabergé">Peter Carl Fabergé</a> - fled Russia to Germany, settled first in Bad Homburg and then in Wiesbaden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schoolboy_Q" title="Schoolboy Q">Quincy Matthew Hanley</a> - American rapper, was born in Wiesbaden (parents were in the military).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexej_von_Jawlensky" title="Alexej von Jawlensky">Alexej von Jawlensky</a> - Russian Expressionist painter, lived there from 1922 until his death in 1941.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Priscilla_Presley" title="Priscilla Presley">Priscilla Presley</a> (Beaulieu at the time) - lived in Wiesbaden with her parents (her father was an Air Force Officer stationed here). It was here that she met <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a> – she was 14 years old at the time, Elvis was 24.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Max_Reger" title="Max Reger">Max Reger</a> - studied in Wiesbaden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mickey_Rourke" title="Mickey Rourke">Mickey Rourke</a> - resides in Wiesbaden at least part-time with his Russian-born girlfriend Anastassija Makarenko.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Debby_Ryan" title="Debby Ryan">Debby Ryan</a> - American actress, lived in Wiesbaden for three years (her father was in the military).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> - settled in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wiesbaden-Biebrich" title="Wiesbaden-Biebrich">Biebrich</a> (now part of Wiesbaden) in 1861, after the political ban against him in Germany was lifted. It was there that he began work on <a href="/wiki/Die_Meistersinger_von_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Die Meistersinger von Nürnberg">Die Meistersinger von Nürnberg</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reese_Witherspoon" title="Reese Witherspoon">Reese Witherspoon</a> - lived in Wiesbaden with her parents (her father worked for the U.S. military here).</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_visitors">Famous visitors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Famous visitors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In the 19th century, visitors to the Wiesbaden's famous hot springs included <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann Wolfgang von Goethe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>. Brahms' <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._3_(Brahms)" title="Symphony No. 3 (Brahms)">Symphony No. 3</a> (Op. 90) was composed in Wiesbaden in the summer of 1883.</li>
<li>Russian author <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky">Fyodor Dostoyevsky</a>, who suffered from an acute gambling compulsion, allegedly lost his travelling money in Wiesbaden's <i>Spielbank</i> casino in 1865. The experience became the inspiration of his 1866 novel <a href="/wiki/The_Gambler_(novel)" title="The Gambler (novel)">The Gambler</a> (Russian Игрок), set in the fictitious place "Roulettenburg". Some historians have disputed this account, saying that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bad_Homburg" title="Bad Homburg">Bad Homburg</a> was the location for Dostoyevsky's real-life misfortune.</li>
<li>Wiesbaden's Bowling Green has been very popular in recent years since various open-air concerts have been held there by artists like <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> (2009 &amp; 2011), <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a> (2009), <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> (2008), <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a> (2003), <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> (2001), <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a> (2000), <a href="/wiki/Simply_Red" title="Simply Red">Simply Red</a> (1999), <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carreras" title="José Carreras">José Carreras</a> (1992) and <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti" title="Luciano Pavarotti">Luciano Pavarotti</a> (1993). <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">Lionel Richie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plácido Domingo">Plácido Domingo</a> (2nd time in Wiesbaden) have also performed there.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalry_with_Mainz">Rivalry with Mainz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Rivalry with Mainz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a>, on the opposite side of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> river, is Wiesbaden's archrival – the two cities are the capitals of their respective Bundesländer, and citizens of both cities <a href="/wiki/Joke" title="Joke">jokingly</a> refer to those on the other one as "living on the wrong side of the river".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fictional_references">Fictional references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wiesbaden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Fictional references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In his short story <a href="/wiki/The_Horror_of_the_Heights" title="The Horror of the Heights">The Horror of the Heights</a> (1913), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Sir Arthur Conan Doyle">Sir Arthur Conan Doyle</a> refers to the <i>Wiesbaden-Homburg Triangle</i> as a region in which aircraft mysteriously vanish.</li>
<li>In the 1983 American television movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Day_After" title="The Day After">The Day After</a></i>, Wiesbaden was the first city to be destroyed by a nuclear weapon during the escalating war between <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> forces that eventually leads to a full-scale nuclear exchange between the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.</li>
<li>The historical novel series <i>Romanike</i> (2006–2014) by Codex Regius features Wiesbaden in the Roman age, or Aquae Mattiacorum, as one of its main locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
